In re New Jersey Firemen's Ass'n Obligation to Provide Relief Applications under Open Public Records Act


DOCKET NO. A-2810-13T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


443 N.J. Super. 238; 128 A.3d 716; 2015 N.J. Super. LEXIS 208


June 2, 2015, Argued 
December 18, 2015, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication December 18, 2015.
Certification granted by In re New Jersey Firemen's Ass'n Obligation to Provide Relief Applications Under Open Public Records Act, 224 N.J. 528, 135 A.3d 148, 2016 N.J. LEXIS 473 (Apr. 25, 2016)
Reversed by N.J. Firemen's Ass'n Obligation v. Doe, 2017 N.J. LEXIS 823 (N.J., Aug. 3, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Union County, Docket No. L-2932-13.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In an Open Public Records Act (OPRA) and common law right of access case, the trial court erred in granting the State Firemen's Association a declaratory judgment that it correctly denied access to records of a relief award to its member; a records custodian could not bring a declaratory judgment action against a record requestor to enforce its right to withhold records, because OPRA did not provide the custodian an independent right of action; [2]-As to both OPRA and the common law, declaratory relief was inappropriate because the declaratory judgment action was essentially an effort to preempt an imminent claim by the records requestor; and allowing a declaratory judgment action solely with respect to the common law would unnecessarily fragment claims; [3]-Both OPRA and the common law required disclosure of documents containing the applicant's name and the award amount.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

194 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sene


DOCKET NO. A-2256-13T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


443 N.J. Super. 134; 128 A.3d 175; 2015 N.J. Super. LEXIS 201


October 7, 2015, Argued 
November 25, 2015, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication November 25, 2015.
Certification denied by State v. Sene, 224 N.J. 282, 132 A.3d 425, 2016 N.J. LEXIS 284 (N.J., Mar. 8, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Atlantic County, Indictment No. 12-08-1914.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Where defendant was driving a taxi when a pedestrian stepped into his lane of traffic, fell into the adjoining lane of traffic and was killed when she was run over by another vehicle, and defendant did not stop his taxi at the scene and left without speaking to anyone, a jury properly convicted him of leaving the scene of a fatal motor vehicle accident under N.J.S.A. § 2C:11-5.1 because contact between defendant's vehicle and the victim was not an element of that crime, and the trial court did not err in declining to instruct the jury that it was; [2]-Section 2C:11-5.1 was not unconstitutionally vague, as the phrase "involved in an accident" was neither vague on its face, nor as applied to defendant; [3]-The trial court erred in failing to correctly identify the aggravating and mitigating factors, and in ordering restitution without conducting a hearing.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's second-degree criminal conviction but vacated the restitution award and remanded the case to the trial court for resentencing and for a hearing on restitution in accordance with N.J.S.A. § 2C:44-2(b), (c).

State in Interest of C.L.H.'s Weapons


DOCKET NO. A-0072-14T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


443 N.J. Super. 48; 126 A.3d 1258; 2015 N.J. Super. LEXIS 196


September 16, 2015, Submitted 
November 18, 2015, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication November 18, 2015.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Family Part, Cumberland County, Docket No. FO-06-254-13.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court erred in denying the State's motion to forfeit weapons under N.J.S.A. 2C:25-28(j) on the ground that the husband was not a defendant in the domestic violence case, and the guns were seized solely because of a restraining order against his wife, and erred in determining the gun amnesty law applied because the weapons were in the possession of the prosecutor on the law's effective date; [2]-As assault firearms were seized under the Prevention of Domestic Violence Act and could not be returned to the husband under the Domestic Violence Forfeiture Statute as they were contraband under N.J.S.A. § 2C:64-1(a)(1), he was disqualified from obtaining a handgun purchase permit or firearms purchaser identification card under the Gun Control Law, N.J.S.A. § 2C:58-3(c)(8), and thus from regaining his remaining firearms and firearms purchaser identification card.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed.

Piatt v. Police & Firemen's Retirement System


DOCKET NO. A-5504-12T1


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


443 N.J. Super. 80; 127 A.3d 716; 2015 N.J. Super. LEXIS 197


April 13, 2015, Argued 
November 18, 2015, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication November 18, 2015.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County, Docket No. L-44-11.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Under N.J.S.A. § 43:16A-3 and N.J.A.C. 17:4-2.5(a), a person could be no more than 35 years old when becoming a member of the Police and Firemen's Retirement System (PFRS); though plaintiff state corrections officers claimed that age requirement did not apply to them, the legislature intended to restrict PFRS membership to persons meeting that age requirement at the time they became a "policeman" or "fireman" (§ 43:16A-3); [2]-Though § 43:16A-3 applied to political subdivisions, it also applied to state corrections officers as the legislature included them in the definition of "policeman"; [3]-The age requirement served legislative goals of using PFRS's heightened benefits to encourage persons to become officers while young and fit, and to retire at a relatively early age, and the PFRS Board, by enacting § 17:4-2.5(a), properly applied this construction of the PFRS Act.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

197 of 1283 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ashley


APPELLATE DIVISION DOCKET NO. A-0403-12T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


443 N.J. Super. 10; 126 A.3d 1234; 2015 N.J. Super. LEXIS 166


March 9, 2015, Submitted 
October 14, 2015, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication October 14, 2015.
Certification denied by State v. Ashley, 2016 N.J. LEXIS 300 (N.J., Mar. 14, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Monmouth County, Indictment No. 03-06-1233.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In a case wherein defendant's guilty plea lacked an adequate factual basis for two of three charges, but after he had been advised by the trial court regarding the maximum sentence the judge was inclined to impose, it was error to deny his motion to vacate his plea and sentence him to the ten year term because it was intended that the maximum ten-year sentence the judge was inclined to impose would globally address all charges and defendant provided an inadequate factual basis for the most serious offenses; [2]-The court held that when there has been a plea agreement and a defendant seeks to withdraw his guilty plea to multiple counts after providing an inadequate factual basis to support the plea, the remedy is to vacate the plea in its entirety, reinstate the dismissed charges and restore both the State and the defendant to their positions prior to the guilty plea.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed; case remanded to trial court for further proceedings.

State v. Nance


DOCKET NO. A-5715-12T3, A-0479-13T3, A-0715-13T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


442 N.J. Super. 268; 122 A.3d 348; 2015 N.J. Super. LEXIS 145


February 3, 2015, Argued 
September 8, 2015, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication September 8, 2015.
Certification granted by State v. Nance, 224 N.J. 124, 129 A.3d 330, 2016 N.J. LEXIS 101 (2016)
Certification granted by, Sub nomine at State v. Willis-Bolton, 224 N.J. 124, 129 A.3d 330, 2016 N.J. LEXIS 117 (2016)
Certification granted by, Sub nomine at State v. Williams, 224 N.J. 124, 129 A.3d 330, 2016 N.J. LEXIS 105 (2016)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by State v. Nance, 2017 N.J. LEXIS 378 (N.J., Apr. 5, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Mercer County, Indictment No. 12-11-0195 in A-5715-12; Monmouth County, Indictment No. 12-02-0380 in A-0479-13; and Union County, Indictment No. 11-04-0471 in A-0715-13.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In consolidated Graves Act, N.J.S.A. § 2C:43-6, cases, the court held that after a motion for waiver by the State was approved by the assignment judge or the designee judge, the sentencing judge, notwithstanding a plea agreement, had the discretion to impose either a probationary sentence or a one-year parole disqualifier; [2]-The court held the plea in such circumstances was not a contract plea and did not have a binding effect on the court.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed; case remanded to trial court for resentencing.

State v. Benjamin


DOCKET NO. A-1569-13T3


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


442 N.J. Super. 258; 122 A.3d 341; 2015 N.J. Super. LEXIS 146


February 3, 2015, Argued 
September 8, 2015, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication September 8, 2015.
Certification granted by, in part State v. Benjamin, 224 N.J. 119, 129 A.3d 326, 2016 N.J. LEXIS 14 (2016)
Affirmed in part and modified in part by State v. Benjamin, 2017 N.J. LEXIS 377 (N.J., Apr. 5, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court of New Jersey, Law Division, Middlesex County, Indictment No. 11-09-1414.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: `HOLDINGS: [1]-The court held that defendant should be given the opportunity to pursue an Alvarez motion, namely, whether the State's decision to not consent to a waiver was arbitrary and discriminatory as the court was persuaded defendant was denied a full and fair opportunity to pursue the Alvarez motion because the State claimed it did not maintain, and thus could not produce, other case files involving waiver decisions despite the Attorney General's Directive requiring the retention of all such files; [2]-The court held that the State shall be required to provide, in writing, the reasons for a denial of a waiver similar to the requirement for Pre-Trial Intervention decision in order to promote procedural fairness and to ensure meaningful judicial review.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed; case remanded to trial court for further proceedings.

J.I. v. New Jersey State Parole Bd.


DOCKET NO. A-1293-14T2


SUPERIOR COURT OF NEW JERSEY, APPELLATE DIVISION


441 N.J. Super. 564; 120 A.3d 256; 2015 N.J. Super. LEXIS 128


April 15, 2015, Argued Telephonically 
August 11, 2015, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Approved for Publication August 11, 2015.
Certification granted by J.I. v. New Jersey State Parole Bd., 223 N.J. 555, 127 A.3d 701, 2015 N.J. LEXIS 1335 (Nov. 17, 2015)
Reversed by, Remanded by J.I. v. New Jersey State Parole Bd., 2017 N.J. LEXIS 315 (N.J., Mar. 21, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the New Jersey State Parole Board.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Appellant was a convicted sex offender monitored by the Parole Board as an offender subject to conditions of community supervision for life (CSL) that banned his use of Internet-capable devices and access to social networking websites and the Internet pursuant to N.J.A.C. § 10A:71-6.11(b)(22) and banned his viewing or possessing pornography and using, possessing and purchasing alcohol; the appellate court rejected his constitutional facial challenges to § 10A:71-6.11(b)(22) for the reasons expressed in J.B. v. N.J. State Parole Bd., and held that this ruling applied to all offenders serving a CSL, regardless of whether their sex crimes were Internet-related; [2]-It rejected his as-applied challenges to the regulation, concluding there was no ex post facto violation; [3]-It concluded the Board's decision to impose the conditions was not arbitrary, capricious or unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
